<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Siberia</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Siberian" redirects here. For the Federal district, see <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Federal_District" title="Siberian Federal District">Siberian Federal District</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Siberia_(disambiguation)" title="Siberia (disambiguation)">Siberia (disambiguation)</a> and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Siberian_(disambiguation)" title="Siberian (disambiguation)">Siberian (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>.</div>
<p>
<span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Siberia&amp;params=60_0_N_105_0_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">60°0′N</span> <span class="longitude">105°0′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">60.000°N 105.000°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">60.000; 105.000</span></span></span></a></span></span></span>
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Geographical region</div><table class="infobox geography vcard" style="width:22em;width:23em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size:1.25em; white-space:nowrap"><div class="fn org" style="display:inline">Siberia</div><br/><div class="nickname" style="font-size:78%;display:inline;"><a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <i><span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">Сибирь</span></i> (<i>Sibirj</i>)</div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#cddeff; font-weight:bold;"><div class="category"><a href="#Geography">Geographical region</a></div></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siberia-FederalSubjects.svg" title="       Siberian Federal District        Geographic Russian Siberia        North Asia"><img alt="       Siberian Federal District        Geographic Russian Siberia        North Asia" data-file-height="630" data-file-width="1092" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Siberia-FederalSubjects.svg/250px-Siberia-FederalSubjects.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Siberia-FederalSubjects.svg/375px-Siberia-FederalSubjects.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Siberia-FederalSubjects.svg/500px-Siberia-FederalSubjects.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a><div style="padding:0.4em 0 0 0;"><span style="margin:0px; position:left; padding-bottom:1px; background-color:#CC0000;">      </span> <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Federal_District" title="Siberian Federal District">Siberian Federal District</a><br/>
<p><span style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:1px;"><span style="border:#CC0000; background-color:#CC0000; color:#CC0000;">   </span><span style="border:#FF4000; background-color:#FF4000; color:#FF4000;">   </span> Geographic Russian Siberia</span><br/>
</p>
<span style="margin:0px; padding-bottom:1px;"><span style="border:#CC0000; background-color:#CC0000; color:#CC0000;">  </span><span style="border:#FF4000; background-color:#FF4000; color:#FF4000;">  </span><span style="border:#FF9933; background-color:#FF9933; color:#FF9933;">  </span> <a href="/wiki/North_Asia" title="North Asia">North Asia</a></span></div></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Country</th><td><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row">Region</th><td><a href="/wiki/North_Asia" title="North Asia">North Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Parts</th><td><b></b><a href="/wiki/West_Siberian_Plain" title="West Siberian Plain">West Siberian Plain</a><br/><a href="/wiki/Central_Siberian_Plateau" title="Central Siberian Plateau">Central Siberian Plateau</a><br/><a href="/wiki/Siberia#Geography" title="Siberia"><i>others...</i></a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left">Area<div style="font-weight:normal;display:inline;"></div></th></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"> • Total</th><td>13,100,000 km<sup>2</sup> (5,100,000 sq mi)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left">Population <div style="font-weight:normal;display:inline;">(2017)</div></th></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"> • Total</th><td>36,000,000</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"> • Density</th><td>2.7/km<sup>2</sup> (7.1/sq mi)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Siberia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɪər/: 'ear' in 'near'">ɪər</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">Сиби́рь</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">tr.</a></small> <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian language text">Sibírj;</i>, <small>IPA: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">[sʲɪˈbʲirʲ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ru-%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%8C.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/79/Ru-%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%8C.ogg" title="Ru-Сибирь.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>) is an extensive geographical <a href="/wiki/Region" title="Region">region</a> spanning much of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Asia" title="North Asia">North Asia</a>. Siberia has historically been a <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_Siberia" title="Russian conquest of Siberia">part of modern Russia</a> since the 16th and 17th centuries.
</p><p>The territory of Siberia extends eastwards from the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Drainage_divide" title="Drainage divide">watershed</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic</a> <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drainage basins</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Yenisei_River" title="Yenisei River">Yenisei River</a> conditionally divides Siberia into two parts, <a href="/wiki/Western_Siberia" title="Western Siberia">Western</a> and Eastern. Siberia stretches southwards from the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a> to the hills of north-central <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> and to the national borders of <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> With an area of 13.1 million square kilometres (5,100,000 sq mi), Siberia accounts for 77% of Russia's land area, but it is home to approximately 36 million people—27% of the country's population. This is equivalent to an average population density of about 3 inhabitants per square kilometre (7.8/sq mi) (approximately equal to that of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>), making Siberia one of the most sparsely populated regions on Earth. If it were a country by itself, it would still be the largest country in area, but in population it would be the world's 35th-largest and Asia's 14th-largest.
</p><p>Worldwide, Siberia is well known primarily for its long, harsh winters, with a January average of −25 °C (−13 °F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> as well as its extensive history of use by Russian and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> administrations as a place for prisons, <a href="/wiki/Gulag#Geography" title="Gulag">labor camps</a>, and exile.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The origin of the name is unknown. Some sources say that "Siberia" originates from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Tatar" title="Siberian Tatar">Siberian Tatar</a> word for "sleeping land" (Sib Ir).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Another account sees the name as the ancient tribal ethnonym of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sirtya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sirtya (page does not exist)">Sirtya</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%82%D1%8F" title="ru:Сиртя">ru</a>]</span> (also "Syopyr" (sʲɵpᵻr)), an ethnic group which spoke a <a href="/wiki/Paleosiberian_languages" title="Paleosiberian languages">Paleosiberian</a> language. The Sirtya people were later assimilated into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Tatar" title="Siberian Tatar">Siberian Tatars</a>.
</p><p>The modern usage of the name was recorded in the Russian language after the Empire's conquest of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Khanate" title="Siberian Khanate">Siberian Khanate</a>. A further variant claims that the region was named after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xibe_people" title="Xibe people">Xibe people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manchus213_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-manchus213-4">[4]</a></sup> The Polish historian Chycliczkowski has proposed that the name derives from the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Slavic" title="Proto-Slavic">proto-Slavic</a> word for "north" (север, <i>sever</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> but Anatole Baikaloff has dismissed this explanation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> He said that the neighbouring Chinese, Turks, and Mongolians, who have similar names for the region, would not have known Russian. He suggests that the name might be a combination of two words with <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a> origin, <i>"su"</i> (water) and <i>"bir"</i> (wild land).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The region has <a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">paleontological</a> significance, as it contains bodies of <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">prehistoric</a> animals from the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> <a href="/wiki/Epoch_(geology)" title="Epoch (geology)">Epoch</a>, preserved in ice or in <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">permafrost</a>. Specimens of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panthera_leo_spelaea#Specimens" title="Panthera leo spelaea">Goldfuss cave lion cubs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yuka_(mammoth)" title="Yuka (mammoth)">Yuka (mammoth)</a> and another <a href="/wiki/Woolly_mammoth" title="Woolly mammoth">woolly mammoth</a> from <a href="/wiki/Oymyakon" title="Oymyakon">Oymyakon</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Woolly_rhinoceros" title="Woolly rhinoceros">woolly rhinoceros</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Kolyma_River" title="Kolyma River">Kolyma River</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bison" title="Bison">bison</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horse" title="Horse">horses</a> from <a href="/wiki/Yukagir" title="Yukagir">Yukagir</a> have been found.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thesiberiantimes2015_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thesiberiantimes2015-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Traps" title="Siberian Traps">Siberian Traps</a> were formed by one of the largest-known volcanic events of the last 500 million years of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_geological_history" title="Earth's geological history">Earth's geological history</a>. Their activity continued for a million years and some scientists consider it a possible cause of the "<a href="/wiki/Permian%E2%80%93Triassic_extinction_event" title="Permian–Triassic extinction event">Great Dying</a>" about 250 million years ago,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> – estimated to have killed 90% of species existing at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>At least three species of human lived in Southern Siberia around 40,000 years ago: <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">H. sapiens</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">H. neanderthalensis</a></i>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denisovans" title="Denisovans">Denisovans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Woman_X_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Woman_X-10">[10]</a></sup>
In 2010 DNA evidence identified the last as a separate species.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Siberia" title="History of Siberia">History of Siberia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_explorers" title="List of Russian explorers">List of Russian explorers</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Choris,_Tschuktschen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="706" data-file-width="1010" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Choris%2C_Tschuktschen.jpg/220px-Choris%2C_Tschuktschen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Choris%2C_Tschuktschen.jpg/330px-Choris%2C_Tschuktschen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Choris%2C_Tschuktschen.jpg/440px-Choris%2C_Tschuktschen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Choris,_Tschuktschen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chukchi_people" title="Chukchi people">Chukchi</a>, one of many <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Siberia" title="Indigenous peoples of Siberia">indigenous peoples of Siberia</a>. Representation of a Chukchi family by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Choris" title="Louis Choris">Louis Choris</a> (1816)</div></div></div>
<p>Siberia was inhabited by different groups of <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomads</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Enets_people" title="Enets people">Enets</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nenets_people" title="Nenets people">Nenets</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uyghur_people" title="Uyghur people">Uyghurs</a>. The Khan of Sibir in the vicinity of modern <a href="/wiki/Tobolsk" title="Tobolsk">Tobolsk</a> was known as a prominent figure who endorsed <a href="/wiki/Kubrat" title="Kubrat">Kubrat</a> as <i>Khagan</i> of <a href="/wiki/Old_Great_Bulgaria" title="Old Great Bulgaria">Old Great Bulgaria</a> in 630. The Mongols conquered a large part of this area early in the 13th century.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_Siberian_route.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Map_Siberian_route.svg/390px-Map_Siberian_route.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Map_Siberian_route.svg/585px-Map_Siberian_route.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Map_Siberian_route.svg/780px-Map_Siberian_route.svg.png 2x" width="390"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_Siberian_route.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The map of the <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Route" title="Siberian Route">Siberian Route</a> in the 18th century (<i>green</i>) and the early 19th century (<i>red</i>).</div></div></div>
<p>With the breakup of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous" title="Autonomous">autonomous</a> <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Sibir" title="Khanate of Sibir">Khanate of Sibir</a> was established in the late 15th century. Turkic-speaking <a href="/wiki/Yakuts" title="Yakuts">Yakut</a> migrated north from the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a> region under pressure from the Mongol tribes during the 13th to 15th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Siberia remained a sparsely populated area. Historian <a href="/wiki/John_F._Richards" title="John F. Richards">John F. Richards</a> wrote: "... it is doubtful that the total early modern Siberian population exceeded 300,000 persons."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>The growing power of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> in the West began to undermine the Siberian Khanate in the 16th century. First, groups of traders and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cossack" title="Cossack">Cossacks</a> began to enter the area. The Russian Army was directed to establish forts farther and farther east to protect new settlers from European Russia. Towns such as <a href="/wiki/Mangazeya" title="Mangazeya">Mangazeya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tara,_Russia" title="Tara, Russia">Tara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yeniseysk" title="Yeniseysk">Yeniseysk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tobolsk" title="Tobolsk">Tobolsk</a> were developed, the last being declared the capital of Siberia. At this time, <i>Sibir</i> was the name of a fortress at Qashlik, near Tobolsk. <a href="/wiki/Gerardus_Mercator" title="Gerardus Mercator">Gerardus Mercator</a>, in a map published in 1595, marks <i>Sibier</i> both as the name of a settlement and of the surrounding territory along a left tributary of the Ob.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Other sources<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2017)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> contend that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xibe_people" title="Xibe people">Xibe</a>, an indigenous <a href="/wiki/Tungusic_peoples" title="Tungusic peoples">Tungusic people</a>, offered fierce resistance to Russian expansion beyond the Urals. Some suggest that the term "Siberia" is a Russification of their ethnonym.
</p><p>By the mid-17th century, Russia had established areas of control that extended to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific" title="Pacific">Pacific</a>. Some 230,000 <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> had settled in Siberia by 1709.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Siberia was a destination for sending <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">exiles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first great modern change in Siberia was the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a>, constructed during 1891–1916. It linked Siberia more closely to the rapidly industrialising Russia of <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">Nicholas II</a>. Around seven million people moved to Siberia from <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">European Russia</a> between 1801 and 1914.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> From 1859 to 1917, more than half a million people migrated to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">Russian Far East</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Siberia has extensive natural resources. During the 20th century, large-scale exploitation of these was developed, and industrial towns cropped up throughout the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novosibirsk-Karimov.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Novosibirsk-Karimov.jpg/220px-Novosibirsk-Karimov.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Novosibirsk-Karimov.jpg/330px-Novosibirsk-Karimov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Novosibirsk-Karimov.jpg/440px-Novosibirsk-Karimov.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Novosibirsk-Karimov.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Siberian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cossack" title="Cossack">Cossack</a> family in <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk" title="Novosibirsk">Novosibirsk</a></div></div></div>
<p>At 7:15 a.m. on 30 June 1908, millions of trees were felled near the <a href="/wiki/Podkamennaya_Tunguska_River" title="Podkamennaya Tunguska River">Podkamennaya Tunguska (Stony Tunguska) River</a> in central Siberia in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tunguska_Event" title="Tunguska Event">Tunguska Event</a>. Most scientists believe this resulted from the air burst of a meteor or a comet. Even though no crater has ever been found, the landscape in the (sparsely inhabited) area still bears the scars of this event.
</p><p>In the early decades of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> (especially the 1930s and 1940s), the government established the <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">Gulag</a> state agency to administer a system of penal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labour_camp" title="Labour camp">labour camps</a>, replacing the previous <a href="/wiki/Katorga" title="Katorga">katorga</a> system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> According to semi-official Soviet estimates, which were not made public until after the fall of the Soviet government, from 1929 to 1953 more than 14 million people passed through these camps and prisons, many of which were in Siberia. Another seven to eight million people were <a href="/wiki/Forced_settlements_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Forced settlements in the Soviet Union">internally deported</a> to remote areas of the Soviet Union (including entire nationalities or ethnicities in several cases).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>Half a million (516,841) prisoners died in camps from 1941 to 1943<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> due to food shortages caused by <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. At other periods, mortality was comparatively lower.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The size, scope, and scale of the Gulag slave labour camps remains a subject of much research and debate. Many Gulag camps were positioned in extremely remote areas of northeastern Siberia. The best known clusters are <i><a href="/wiki/Sevvostlag" title="Sevvostlag">Sevvostlag</a></i> (<i>The North-East Camps</i>) along the <a href="/wiki/Kolyma" title="Kolyma">Kolyma</a> River and <i><a href="/wiki/Norillag" title="Norillag">Norillag</a></i> near <a href="/wiki/Norilsk" title="Norilsk">Norilsk</a>, where 69,000 prisoners were kept in 1952.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Major industrial cities of Northern Siberia, such as <a href="/wiki/Norilsk" title="Norilsk">Norilsk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magadan" title="Magadan">Magadan</a>, developed from camps built by prisoners and run by former prisoners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Russia" title="Geography of Russia">Geography of Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Asia#Geography" title="North Asia">North Asia § Geography</a></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koryaksky_volcano_Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky_oct-2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="954" data-file-width="1272" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Koryaksky_volcano_Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky_oct-2005.jpg/220px-Koryaksky_volcano_Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky_oct-2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Koryaksky_volcano_Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky_oct-2005.jpg/330px-Koryaksky_volcano_Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky_oct-2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Koryaksky_volcano_Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky_oct-2005.jpg/440px-Koryaksky_volcano_Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky_oct-2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koryaksky_volcano_Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky_oct-2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Koryaksky" title="Koryaksky">Koryaksky</a> volcano towering over <a href="/wiki/Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky" title="Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky">Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Kamchatka_Peninsula" title="Kamchatka Peninsula">Kamchatka Peninsula</a></div></div></div>
<p>With an area of 13.1 million square kilometres (5,100,000 sq mi), Siberia makes up roughly 77% of Russia's total territory and almost 10% of Earth's land surface (148,940,000 km<sup>2</sup>, 57,510,000 sq mi). While Siberia falls entirely within Asia, many authorities such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_geoscheme" title="UN geoscheme">UN geoscheme</a> will not subdivide countries and will place all of Russia as part of Europe and/or <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>. Major geographical zones include the <a href="/wiki/West_Siberian_Plain" title="West Siberian Plain">West Siberian Plain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Central_Siberian_Plateau" title="Central Siberian Plateau">Central Siberian Plateau</a>.
</p><p>Eastern and central <a href="/wiki/Sakha_Republic" title="Sakha Republic">Sakha</a> comprises numerous north-south mountain ranges of various ages. These mountains extend up to almost 3,000 metres (9,800 ft), but above a few hundred metres they are almost completely devoid of vegetation. The <a href="/wiki/Verkhoyansk_Range" title="Verkhoyansk Range">Verkhoyansk Range</a> was extensively glaciated in the Pleistocene, but the climate was too dry for glaciation to extend to low elevations. At these low elevations are numerous valleys, many of them deep and covered with <a href="/wiki/Larch" title="Larch">larch</a> forest, except in the extreme north where the <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> dominates. Soils are mainly turbels (a type of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gelisols" title="Gelisols">gelisol</a>). The active layer tends to be less than one metre deep, except near rivers.
</p><p>The highest point in Siberia is the active <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> <a href="/wiki/Klyuchevskaya_Sopka" title="Klyuchevskaya Sopka">Klyuchevskaya Sopka</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Kamchatka_Peninsula" title="Kamchatka Peninsula">Kamchatka Peninsula</a>. Its peak is at 4,750 metres (15,580 ft).
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grasslands">Grasslands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Grasslands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ukok_Plateau" title="Ukok Plateau">Ukok Plateau</a> — part of a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The West Siberian Plain consists mostly of <a href="/wiki/Cenozoic" title="Cenozoic">Cenozoic</a> alluvial deposits and is somewhat flat. Many deposits on this plain result from <a href="/wiki/Proglacial_lake" title="Proglacial lake">ice dams</a> which produced a large <a href="/wiki/Glacial_lake" title="Glacial lake">glacial lake</a>. This mid- to late-<a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> lake blocked the northward flow of the <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">Ob</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yenisei_River" title="Yenisei River">Yenisei</a> rivers, resulting in a redirection southwest into the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral</a> seas via the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turgai_Valley" title="Turgai Valley">Turgai Valley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The area is very swampy, and soils are mostly peaty <a href="/wiki/Histosol" title="Histosol">histosols</a> and, in the treeless northern part, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Histels" title="Histels">histels</a>. In the south of the plain, where <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">permafrost</a> is largely absent, rich grasslands that are an extension of the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Steppe" title="Kazakh Steppe">Kazakh Steppe</a> formed the original vegetation, most of which is no longer visible.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The reason for this is unclear. (April 2015)">why?</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The Central Siberian Plateau is an ancient <a href="/wiki/Craton" title="Craton">craton</a> (sometimes named <i>Angaraland</i>) that formed an independent <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a> before the <a href="/wiki/Permian" title="Permian">Permian</a> (see the <a href="/wiki/Siberia_(continent)" title="Siberia (continent)">Siberian continent</a>). It is exceptionally rich in minerals, containing large deposits of <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamonds</a>, and ores of <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Molybdenum" title="Molybdenum">molybdenum</a>. Much of the area includes the <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Traps" title="Siberian Traps">Siberian Traps</a>—a <a href="/wiki/Large_igneous_province" title="Large igneous province">large igneous province</a>. This massive eruptive period was approximately coincident with the <a href="/wiki/Permian%E2%80%93Triassic_extinction_event" title="Permian–Triassic extinction event">Permian–Triassic extinction event</a>. The volcanic event is said to be the largest known <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanic_eruption" title="Volcanic eruption">volcanic eruption</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Earth" title="History of the Earth">Earth's history</a>. Only the extreme northwest was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glaciated" title="Glaciated">glaciated</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">Quaternary</a>, but almost all is under exceptionally deep permafrost, and the only <a href="/wiki/Tree" title="Tree">tree</a> that can thrive, despite the warm summers, is the deciduous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Larch" title="Siberian Larch">Siberian Larch</a> (<i>Larix sibirica</i>) with its very shallow roots. Outside the extreme northwest, the <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">taiga</a> is dominant, covering a significant fraction of the entirety of Siberia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Soils here are mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gelisols" title="Gelisols">turbels</a>, giving way to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spodosols" title="Spodosols">spodosols</a> where the active layer becomes thicker and the ice content lower.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Akkem_Valley_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2784" data-file-width="4176" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Akkem_Valley_2011.jpg/220px-Akkem_Valley_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Akkem_Valley_2011.jpg/330px-Akkem_Valley_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Akkem_Valley_2011.jpg/440px-Akkem_Valley_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akkem_Valley_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Belukha_Mountain" title="Belukha Mountain">Belukha Mountain</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/%D0%9E%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_%D0%B2_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D1%8B%D1%85_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD%2C_%D0%91%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F%2C_%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F.jpg/330px-%D0%9E%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_%D0%B2_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D1%8B%D1%85_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD%2C_%D0%91%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F%2C_%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/%D0%9E%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_%D0%B2_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D1%8B%D1%85_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD%2C_%D0%91%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F%2C_%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F.jpg/440px-%D0%9E%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_%D0%B2_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D1%8B%D1%85_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD%2C_%D0%91%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F%2C_%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9E%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%81_%D0%B2_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%85_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D1%8B%D1%85_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD,_%D0%91%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F,_%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%8F.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Autumn forest in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Sayan_Mountains" title="Sayan Mountains">Sayan Mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buryatia" title="Buryatia">Buryatia</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <i>Lena-Tunguska petroleum province</i> includes the Central Siberian platform (some authors refer to it as the Eastern Siberian platform), bounded on the northeast and east by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Carboniferous" title="Late Carboniferous">Late Carboniferous</a> through <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> Verkhoyansk <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foldbelt" title="Foldbelt">foldbelt</a>, on the northwest by the <a href="/wiki/Paleozoic" title="Paleozoic">Paleozoic</a> Taymr foldbelt, and on the southeast, south and southwest by the Middle <a href="/wiki/Silurian" title="Silurian">Silurian</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Devonian" title="Middle Devonian">Middle Devonian</a> Baykalian foldbelt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meyerhof_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Meyerhof-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>228</span></sup> A regional geologic reconnaissance study begun in 1932, followed by surface and subsurface mapping, revealed the Markova-Angara Arch (<a href="/wiki/Anticline" title="Anticline">anticline</a>). This led to the discovery of the Markovo Oil Field in 1962 with the Markovo 1 well, which produced from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Cambrian" title="Early Cambrian">Early Cambrian</a> Osa Horizon <a href="/wiki/Shoal" title="Shoal">bar</a>-<a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> at a depth of 2,156 metres (7,073 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meyerhof_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Meyerhof-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>243</span></sup> The <i>Sredne-Botuobin Gas Field</i> was discovered in 1970, producing from the Osa and the <a href="/wiki/Proterozoic" title="Proterozoic">Proterozoic</a> Parfenovo Horizon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meyerhof_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-Meyerhof-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>244</span></sup> The Yaraktin Oil Field was discovered in 1971, producing from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vendian" title="Vendian">Vendian</a> Yaraktin Horizon at depths of up to 1,750 metres (5,740 ft), which lies below <a href="/wiki/Permian" title="Permian">Permian</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_Jurassic" title="Lower Jurassic">Lower Jurassic</a> <a href="/wiki/Flood_basalt" title="Flood basalt">basalt traps</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meyerhof_28-3"><a href="#cite_note-Meyerhof-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>244</span></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Russia" title="Climate of Russia">Climate of Russia</a></div>
<table style="width: 800px;">

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>
<p><span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:#c0c0c0; color:#c0c0c0;">    </span> polar desert</span>

</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">Vegetation</a> in Siberia is mostly <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">taiga</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> belt on the northern fringe, and a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forest" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forest">temperate forest</a> zone in the south.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The climate of Siberia varies dramatically, but it typically has short summers and long, brutally cold winters. On the north coast, north of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Circle" title="Arctic Circle">Arctic Circle</a>, there is a very short (about one-month-long) summer.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BaikalForest_(pixinn.net).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="718" decoding="async" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/BaikalForest_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/170px-BaikalForest_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/BaikalForest_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/255px-BaikalForest_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/BaikalForest_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/340px-BaikalForest_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BaikalForest_(pixinn.net).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">Taiga</a> near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a></div></div></div>
<p>Almost all the population lives in the south, along the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a>. The climate in this southernmost part is <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">Humid continental climate</a> (Köppen <i>Dfb</i>) with cold winters but fairly warm summers lasting at least four months. The annual average is about 0.5 °C (32.9 °F). January averages about −20 °C (−4 °F) and July about +19 °C (66 °F) while daytime temperatures in summer typically are above 20 °C (68 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> With a reliable growing season, an abundance of sunshine and exceedingly fertile <a href="/wiki/Chernozem" title="Chernozem">chernozem</a> soils, southern Siberia is good enough for profitable <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, as was proven in the early 20th century.
</p><p>By far the most commonly occurring climate in Siberia is continental <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic</a> (Koppen <i>Dfc</i> or <i>Dwc</i>), with the annual average temperature about −5 °C (23 °F) and an average for January of −25 °C (−13 °F) and an average for July of +17 °C (63 °F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> although this varies considerably, with a July average about 10 °C (50 °F) in the taiga–tundra <a href="/wiki/Ecotone" title="Ecotone">ecotone</a>. The Business oriented website and blog <i>Business Insider</i> lists <a href="/wiki/Verkhoyansk" title="Verkhoyansk">Verkhoyansk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oymyakon" title="Oymyakon">Oymyakon</a>, in Siberia's <a href="/wiki/Sakha_Republic" title="Sakha Republic">Sakha Republic</a>, as being in competition for the title of the Northern Hemisphere's <i><a href="/wiki/Pole_of_Cold" title="Pole of Cold">Pole of Cold</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Oymyakon" title="Oymyakon">Oymyakon</a> is a village which recorded a temperature of −67.7 °C (−89.9 °F) on 6 February 1933. <a href="/wiki/Verkhoyansk" title="Verkhoyansk">Verkhoyansk</a>, a town further north and further inland, recorded a temperature of −69.8 °C (−93.6 °F) for 3 consecutive nights: 5, 6 and 7 February 1933. Each town is alternately considered the Northern Hemisphere's Pole of Cold, meaning the coldest inhabited point in the Northern hemisphere. Each town also frequently reaches 86 °F (30 °C) in the summer, giving them, and much of the rest of Russian Siberia, the world's greatest temperature variation between summer's highs and winter's lows, often being well over 170–180+ °F (94–100+ °C) between the seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> The rural locality of <a href="/wiki/Delyankir" title="Delyankir">Delyankir</a>, also in the Sakha Republic, is another candidate for the "Northern Pole of Cold", as its average temperature throughout all winter months is lower than that of either Oymyakon or Verkhoyansk, and it also has a lower yearly average temperature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weather_Atlas_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weather_Atlas-33">[33]</a></sup> Its record low of −65 °C (−85 °F) is slightly higher than the record lows set at Oymyakon and Verkhoyansk, however.
</p><p>Southwesterly winds bring warm air from Central Asia and the Middle East. The climate in West Siberia (Omsk, Novosibirsk) is several degrees warmer than in the East (Irkutsk, Chita) where in the north an extreme winter subarctic climate (Köppen <i>Dfd</i> or <i>Dwd</i>) prevails. But summer temperatures in other regions can reach +38 °C (100 °F). In general, <a href="/wiki/Sakha_Republic" title="Sakha Republic">Sakha</a> is the coldest Siberian region, and the basin of the <a href="/wiki/Yana_River" title="Yana River">Yana River</a> has the lowest temperatures of all, with permafrost reaching 1,493 metres (4,898 ft). Nevertheless, as far as Imperial Russian plans of settlement were concerned, cold was never viewed as an impediment. In the winter, southern Siberia sits near the center of the semi-permanent <a href="/wiki/Siberian_High" title="Siberian High">Siberian High</a>, so winds are usually light in the winter.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> in Siberia is generally low, exceeding 500 millimetres (20 in) only in <a href="/wiki/Kamchatka_Peninsula" title="Kamchatka Peninsula">Kamchatka</a> where moist winds flow from the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a> onto high mountains – producing the region's only major <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a>, though volcanic eruptions and low summer temperatures allow limited forests to grow. Precipitation is high also in most of <a href="/wiki/Primorsky_Krai" title="Primorsky Krai">Primorye</a> in the extreme south where monsoonal influences can produce quite heavy summer rainfall.
</p>

</td>
<td style="background: #C6FFC6; color:#000000;">38<br/>(1.5)
</td>
<td style="background: #CDFFCD; color:#000000;">32<br/>(1.3)
</td>
<td style="background: #DBFFDB; color:#000000;">24<br/>(0.9)
</td>
<td style="background: #C7FFC7; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">442<br/>(17.4)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Гидрометцентр_России_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Гидрометцентр_России-34">[34]</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Researchers, including Sergei Kirpotin at <a href="/wiki/Tomsk_State_University" title="Tomsk State University">Tomsk State University</a> and Judith Marquand at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxford_University" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a>, warn that <a href="/wiki/West_Siberian_Plain" title="West Siberian Plain">Western Siberia</a> has begun to thaw as a result of <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>. The frozen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peat_bog" title="Peat bog">peat bogs</a> in this region may hold billions of tons of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methane_gas" title="Methane gas">methane gas</a>, which may be released into the atmosphere. Methane is a <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_potential" title="Global warming potential">22 times more powerful</a> than <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In 2008, a research expedition for the <a href="/wiki/American_Geophysical_Union" title="American Geophysical Union">American Geophysical Union</a> detected levels of methane up to 100 times above normal in the atmosphere above the Siberian <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a>, likely the result of <a href="/wiki/Methane_clathrate" title="Methane clathrate">methane clathrates</a> being released through holes in a frozen 'lid' of seabed <a href="/wiki/Permafrost" title="Permafrost">permafrost</a>, around the outfall of the <a href="/wiki/Lena_River" title="Lena River">Lena River</a> and the area between the <a href="/wiki/Laptev_Sea" title="Laptev Sea">Laptev Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Siberian_Sea" title="East Siberian Sea">East Siberian Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Siberian_ethnic_faces">Siberian ethnic faces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Siberian ethnic faces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are at least three different types of faces in Siberian tribes &amp; ethnicities. Similar to the slant eyes (single-eyelids) by East Asians, many Siberians have slit-eyes (single-eyelids). However, there are other distinct looking facial phenotypes in Siberia; many Siberians have big eyes with double-eyelids as well as big &amp; lofty nasal bridge (some Siberians even show dark or red skin) not observable from the other half of Siberians nor from East Asia. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In Siberia, there are typically Eskimo face (Y-Haplogroup C), Turkic face (Y-Haplogroup N), Slavic face (Y-Haplogroup R) as well as many faces somewhere in between due to Mendel's laws. Siberian faces depend on the mixture ratio. Such variety of facial phenotypes are visible even in Chukchi ethnicity which is located at the farthest Eastern Siberia near Alaska. Some East Asian ethnicities such as Northern China &amp; Korea are mixed with these Siberians and show similar faces. Many Siberian ethnicities show higher percentage of Y-Haplogroup N than Mongol; only about 1 out of 10 Mongolians are Turkic (Y-haplogroup N) while the rest of them are mostly Eskimo (Y-haplogroup C) &amp; East Asian (Y-haplogroup O).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Siberian_regionalism" title="Siberian regionalism">Siberian regionalism</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Borders_and_administrative_division">Borders and administrative division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Borders and administrative division">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siberian_Cities_Map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="447" data-file-width="974" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Siberian_Cities_Map.svg/400px-Siberian_Cities_Map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Siberian_Cities_Map.svg/600px-Siberian_Cities_Map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Siberian_Cities_Map.svg/800px-Siberian_Cities_Map.svg.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siberian_Cities_Map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="external text" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1a/Siberian_Cities_Map.svg">Map of the most populated area of Siberia</a> with clickable city names (SVG)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siberian_Cities_Graph.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="453" data-file-width="729" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Siberian_Cities_Graph.svg/400px-Siberian_Cities_Graph.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Siberian_Cities_Graph.svg/600px-Siberian_Cities_Graph.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Siberian_Cities_Graph.svg/800px-Siberian_Cities_Graph.svg.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siberian_Cities_Graph.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="external text" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/66/Siberian_Cities_Graph.svg">Comparison of the nine biggest Siberian cities' growth in the 20th century</a></div></div></div>
<p>The term "Siberia" has a long history. Its meaning has gradually changed during ages. Historically, Siberia was defined as the whole part of Russia to the east of <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">Russian Far East</a>. According to this definition, Siberia extended eastward from the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> to the Pacific coast, and southward from the Arctic Ocean to the border of Russian <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> and the national borders of both Mongolia and China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>Soviet-era sources (<i><a href="/wiki/Great_Soviet_Encyclopedia" title="Great Soviet Encyclopedia">Great Soviet Encyclopedia</a></i> and others)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> and modern Russian ones<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> usually define Siberia as a region extending eastward from the Ural Mountains to the <a href="/wiki/Drainage_divide" title="Drainage divide">watershed</a> between <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic</a> drainage basins, and southward from the Arctic Ocean to the hills of north-central <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> and the national borders of both <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. By this definition, Siberia includes the <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">federal subjects</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Federal_District" title="Siberian Federal District">Siberian Federal District</a>, and some of the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Federal_District" title="Ural Federal District">Ural Federal District</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Sakha_Republic" title="Sakha Republic">Sakha (Yakutia) Republic</a>, which is a part of the <a href="/wiki/Far_Eastern_Federal_District" title="Far Eastern Federal District">Far Eastern Federal District</a>. Geographically, this definition includes subdivisions of several other subjects of Urals and Far Eastern federal districts, but they are not included administratively. This definition excludes <a href="/wiki/Sverdlovsk_Oblast" title="Sverdlovsk Oblast">Sverdlovsk Oblast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chelyabinsk_Oblast" title="Chelyabinsk Oblast">Chelyabinsk Oblast</a>, both of which are included in some wider definitions of Siberia.
</p><p>Other sources may use either a somewhat wider definition that states the Pacific coast, not the watershed, is the eastern boundary (thus including the whole Russian Far East)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> or a somewhat narrower one that limits Siberia to the Siberian Federal District (thus excluding all subjects of other districts).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In Russian, the word for Siberia is used as a substitute for the name of the federal district by those who live in the district itself and less commonly used to denote the federal district by people residing outside of it.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9E%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%8F%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%8C%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_(%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BD-%D0%A3%D0%B4%D1%8D).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="403" data-file-width="604" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/%D0%9E%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%8F%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%8C%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%28%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BD-%D0%A3%D0%B4%D1%8D%29.jpg/220px-%D0%9E%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%8F%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%8C%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%28%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BD-%D0%A3%D0%B4%D1%8D%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/%D0%9E%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%8F%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%8C%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%28%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BD-%D0%A3%D0%B4%D1%8D%29.jpg/330px-%D0%9E%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%8F%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%8C%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%28%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BD-%D0%A3%D0%B4%D1%8D%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/%D0%9E%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%8F%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%8C%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%28%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BD-%D0%A3%D0%B4%D1%8D%29.jpg/440px-%D0%9E%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%8F%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%8C%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%28%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BD-%D0%A3%D0%B4%D1%8D%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9E%D0%BA%D1%82%D1%8F%D0%B1%D1%80%D1%8C%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_(%D0%A3%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BD-%D0%A3%D0%B4%D1%8D).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ulan-Ude" title="Ulan-Ude">Ulan-Ude</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9E%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%804.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2912" data-file-width="4368" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/%D0%9E%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%804.jpg/220px-%D0%9E%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%804.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/%D0%9E%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%804.jpg/330px-%D0%9E%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%804.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/%D0%9E%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%804.jpg/440px-%D0%9E%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%804.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9E%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%804.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk" title="Novosibirsk">Novosibirsk</a> is the largest city in Siberia</div></div></div>
